In desperation I turned to amazon to see if there was such a thing as at home waxing. Enter this GiGi kit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First - my kit came complete and everything worked. No broken parts, spilled bottles, etc. All good. It was easy to set up - but did take much longer to get the wax hot than it said (took me almost an hour). Once it got hot I put it on Low for 15 minutes and was ready to start.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Second - this stuff is MESSY. Very very messy - at least when doing a Brazilian by yourself. While some areas were very simple others were nearly impossible - and clumps of hair were the most difficult to get effectively - especially as the journey took me further down and under. It took 1/2 the container to do a full Brazilian including the butt strip part (and surrounding area). Unfortunately this wax sticks something terrible. About mid way through I switched from the oil provided to baby powder (which is what my wax lady uses) and that was markedly better. Still the under area was a real bear to do. The heat level of the warmer was just right and I had no issues. No ingrowns that I can see - and very smooth areas after wax. In terms of pain I&#x27;m a masochist so it didn&#x27;t bother me much at all.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Third - my lessons learned. Make sure you hold the skin taut - it just doesn&#x27;t work if you don&#x27;t. Do put the wax on in the direction of hair but NEVER stop wax in a group of hair...you will be sorry. Try talcum or baby power instead of the oil if that doesn&#x27;t work as well as you want. Put a big towel outyou don&#x27;t care about as it&#x27;s gonna get wrecked. WEAR GLOVES - you will thank me later. Use smaller sticks in areas you cannot see - better to do smaller bits at a time than big globs that get stuck. Don&#x27;t wait too long to pull it off or it glops up and you cannot get it off. Use the cooling gel after - It really did help.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Good luck! Overall I am VERY happy with this kit. I am saving about $65-100 a visit using this even with the warmer cost. Well worth it!</li>

Start the wax out a bit past the hair line so you can lift up an edge and get the &amp;#34;tear away&amp;#34; process started before the real hairs are pulled up.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Sometimes pulling against the growth of the hair isn&#x27;t what&#x27;s going to get the hairs out (especially true in the armpit area) so wait a few moments, reapply the wax and try again, pulling they wax in the opposite direction, if you see that the hair didn&#x27;t come out the first time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you have gel nails, USE GLOVES.  This stuff can wreck gel polish and probably regular polish too.  I use medical latex gloves and they work fine.  If you do get some gel on your polish, wait until it dries before trying to pick it off.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I found that the first time I do an area is the most painful.  The armpits were THE WORST.  But every subsequent time has been less painful.  Also the hair seems to grow in softer so maybe that&#x27;s why.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If there is any residual wax left it will pick up the colors of the clothing fibers you wear.  For instance if you do your bikini line and wear black undies and PJ pants that night, the residual wax will be black the next day.  Worth mentioning if you do the wax one day and are expecting to be seen naked that night...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am medium skin toned and have only slightly sensitive skin and I get a considerable amount of red, bubbled up skin after a waxing session.  By the next morning it has lessened greatly and it&#x27;s gone within two days time.  Again worth mentioning if you intend to be seen naked that night...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Any residual wax does come off on its own after a couple of days time and a couple of showers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall this kit has been great.  I recently tried waxing my upper lip and it worked just fine there too.  Will keep buying replacement cans!of the clothing fibers you wear.     <li> I really wanted to like this waxing kit -- in fact, I liked it a lot when I first got it and used it. The warmer works well, the wax tore off tons of hair once I watched the video a few times and got the technique down.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;About 3 hours later, however, I was in allergic contact dermatitis hell.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you get skin irritation, rashes, welts, etc. from bandaids, plasters, bandage adhesive, medical tape, or whatever else is similar, or rosin, colophony, etc., do NOT use the Brazilian Hard Body Wax that comes with this!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I get bad rashes and angry, red, raised welts from most self-stick bandages and medical tape. I had no idea that usually the culprit is the sticky rosin or colophony that causes the reaction. That also happens to be the #1 ingredient in this hard wax. :(&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Luckily as a waxing noobie, I only practiced a little on 1 leg and then did both underarms and a bit on one side of my face before I got tired. My armpits are mostly flaring around the edges -- where the hair was thickest and my skin the wrinkliest was luckily spared. My leg took a day to break out in a rash, but now I&#x27;ve got lots of mottled skin, red marks, and pinpricks that are probably from scratching.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you wind up reacting to this wax, my advice is to self-medicate with Benadryl internally and hydrocortisone 1% topically. I kept myself in a self-indued semi-coma, sleeping the better part of 2 days with the help of Benadryl. I applied hydrocortisone to all irritated areas 4 times a day (sometimes more, if it was really itchy.) There are creams, sprays, liquid rollerballs, and cooling hydrocortisone forumlas -- I&#x27;ve been using various combinations of all 4 to keep my scratching to a minimum.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ll be proceeding to an allergist and/or dermatologist as soon as I can get someone to fit me in.     <li> I have really coarse hair &amp;#34;down there&amp;#34; and have tried soo many different hair removal products, all of them resulting in nothing but painful horror stories. This wax WORKS, and it works well, as long as you take the time to learn how to use it the correct way. I cannot emphasize enough the importance of taking the time to lean the correct skills and techniques.  I spent a lot of time reading reviews and watching youtube videos on how to use hard wax, and it spared me the frustration and sticky messes other people experienced.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have never removed all of the hair from my bikini area before, and I have to admit, I&#x27;m doing little sections every few days instead of everything all at once.  After I&#x27;ve done so much waxing, the entire area gets very tender and sore and I just prefer giving my skin a break. Once the hair starts growing back in and its thinner I&#x27;ll be able to do it all in one shot.  It is extremely painful removing all of the hair for the first time, but this is to be expected.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here are a few tips and things I&#x27;ve learned along the way:&lt;br /&gt;-Before doing anything with the wax, watch the video that comes with the kit. Taking the time to do this will spare you sticky messes and an unsuccessful experience.&lt;br /&gt;-ALWAYS take ibuprofen about an hour before waxing.  It will still be extremely painful, but slightly less so than if you were to wax without it. You may also need to take it the day after waxing.  Your skin will be tender for a few days, and quite possibly bruised if you are doing a full brazilian.&lt;br /&gt;-To heat up the wax, turn the warmer on high for approximately 15 minutes, and then to low.  I have never waited for the wax to completely melt before beginning.  Personally, I prefer the thicker texture the wax has when its still melting in the middle.&lt;br /&gt;-The wax is so much easier to use when it is on the thick side. This helps to prevent dripping when you are spreading the wax and makes it easier to spread and keep it only where you want it.&lt;br /&gt;-Use the pre epilation oil, but not too much. Not using it opens up the door to ripping your skin off along with your hair and using too much could prevent the wax from properly adhering to your hair.&lt;br /&gt;-When applying the wax, spread it evenly (in the direction of your hair growth) and DO NOT spread out the edges.  You want the wax to be about an eighth of an inch thick in the middle and thicker on the edges.  I learned from watching videos that this helps to maintain the structure of the wax and will prevent leftover bits from sticking to your skin when you rip it off.&lt;br /&gt;-If you are using the wax for the first time, make sure you practice on your legs or arms first.  You DO NOT want to learn on your bikini area; this could easily result in painful mistakes and lots of sticky wax in areas you really do not want it to be.&lt;br /&gt;-Remove excess bits of wax with baby oil, and do this while the wax is still slightly soft.  Once it is hard, the only thing you can do is pick at it or rip out the hair that it is sticking to.&lt;br /&gt;-A few people mentioned that they strain and reuse their wax.  This is tempting because it saves money, however I would not recommend it.  Doing this can promote bacterial growth in your wax, and you DO NOT want this to happen.  Freshly waxed skin is extremely prone to infection, so keeping your supplies and tools clean and sanitary is incredibly important.  The last thing you want is to end up in the hospital with an infection because you were not keeping your supplies sanitary.&lt;br /&gt;-Inform yourself about how to care for post waxed skin before beginning.  Like I said, freshly waxed skin is extremely prone to infection, and it needs to be taken care of properly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All that being said, I really do love this product. I am SO excited that I&#x27;ve finally found something that works and works well.  Buying the kit was especially handy, and the warmer is so much better than going back and forth between the bathroomand the microwave. Even though the wax is mean specifically for coarse hair, I have used it on my upper lip and eyebrows with success.  It is significantly less painful that the wax strips I typically use.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I would most definitely recommend this kit to anyone who prefers waxing in the comfort of your home and is patient enough to take the time to learn to use this product properly.</li>

Then I stirred a little because the edges warm first, then let it melt some more. I turned it to medium once it was about 85% melted, stirred and tested it on my wrist. Not only was this good for temperature, but I put enough on to make a little strip and got some practice waiting the right amount of time before flicking up an end and ripping off. I found that the lower abdomen hair was MUCH more painful to pull out than those further down or on the sides. Little dots of blood are normal as you are ripping out very thick hair; just keep a paper towel on hand and blot (don&#x27;t wipe!) as needed. Without a strip, you need to work in short 1/2 to 1 1/2 inch areas. It&#x27;s probably better to learn the stripless method (economically and ecologically speaking).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The downside to this wax&#x27;s amazing sticking power is that it likes to leave teeny, tiny little sticky remnants all over. Sugar waxes spoil you with how easy they are to clean up: just wash away! With this stuff, you&#x27;ll think you&#x27;ve gotten all of it off and then find weird little lint-spots on your skin later that day. Not especially great when you&#x27;ve just waxed your face and then you have a cotton ball fuzz mustache.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One thing I don&#x27;t like about the kit is that, as with every other Gigi waxing kit, it recommends using the Pre-Hon cleanser. Unlike every other Gigi waxing kit, it does not come with said cleanser. It also does not come with the Slow-Grow treatment for after waxing.</li>

    <li> Love this kit.    Not very many reviews from husbands waxing their wives, but here goes.  My wife was getting REALLY furry down south, and she agreed to do a Brazilian to spice things up.  No way in hell was she going to go to a salon, though, so it was DIY or nothing.  I couldn&#x27;t see her contorting herself for my pleasure, so I volunteered to do the deed.  After all, it&#x27;s my play area :).    I did a bit of research and watched a few YouTube videos, along with the video that came with the kit.  We set up on a towel on the bed and went to town.  I started with small strips first, then worked up to multiple, longer strips-- applying one, letting one cool, and ripping off the third. There was hardly any pain--except when I forgot to start a strip on a hairless area.  Now my wife has a really high pain tolerance, so I&#x27;m not recommending you do this if it&#x27;s your first time, and you&#x27;re really hairy down there. Some of the strips I pulled had HUNDREDS of hairs (with follicles attached!) on them.  Most of the stuff I read and saw recommended getting it done professionally first, then using the kit to do maintenance procedures on the fewer, finer hairs that regrow after a few weeks.    Tips:    Cooler wax is better than hot wax.  It should form a ball on the stick after spinning it a couple times.  If it runs off the stick, it&#x27;s too hot.  Apply the strip about the thickness of a nickel.    Pay attention to direction of hair growth. You ladies grow hair every which way down there.  Apply back and forth along and against the direction of growth, but yank against the direction of growth.  If you don&#x27;t pull against the direction of growth, you can end up with hair on the strip, but no follicles. You know what that means:  stubble in 48 hours. Oh, and be sure to pull the skin tight while applying the wax.    Pull the skin tight when yanking the strip, then press your hand on the area you just denuded.  The pressure reduces the pain a lot.    Biggie!  Make your strips start from an area of no hair.  This lets you easily pull up the end to get ready to yank without pulling hairs out in slow motion.  I almost got smacked for that one.  Try to leave a tag, or thicker spot on the end where you&#x27;ll be grabbing it.    We found that cornstarch worked better (less pain, more hair removed) than the pre-epilation oil.  YMMV.    Exfoliate and use some sort of growth inhibitor to minimize ingrown hairs.  We use Completely Bare Hair Growth Inhibitor, and have not had a single ingrown hair.    All in all, it took ~90 minutes to tame the beast.  I expect the next session will be half that, now that I have the hang of it.    Oh the hardest part for me?  Waiting 24 hours to play with my masterpiece ;).    ...and why on Earth didn&#x27;t we do this sooner?</li>

Then next few times I shower, I exfoliate and use the gel/baby powder again. The ingrown hairs are much, much better! The real trick is to use the wax when it is not runny at all. It should be \\&quot;gloopy\\&quot;. I heat it for a little while on hot, then to extra low. Sometimes I even turn it off for a few minutes. The wax does not need to cool very much before you pull it off again. If you wait too long, it will obviously harden too much. Also, you will learn that you need some \\&quot;lead area\\&quot; (i.e. a hairless starting point) for getting a grip on the wax. So, apply it so the end where you&#x27;re going to grab it and pull is just outside the hair growth, and that&#x27;s where you&#x27;ll hang onto it to remove it. Way less painful that way.  If something goes wrong, you always use a small piece of wax from a previous pull, and it will stick to the end you want to remove- like a handle, for generating better leverage.</li>

Hopefully the tips below help other beginners.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some tips:&lt;br /&gt;* Watch some youtube videos (and/or the DVD) or get it done professionally first.&lt;br /&gt;* Use a towel or a beadsheet to cover the area you&#x27;ll be in.&lt;br /&gt;* Have a waste basket ready and no distractions.&lt;br /&gt;* Baby powder helps the wax not stick to the skin (I had a little piece of skin get ripped off without the powder - ouch!).&lt;br /&gt;* The pre epilation oil not only reduces the pain by more than half, it also keeps the wax as one big piece and prevents it from sticking to the skin. Here are some tips:&lt;br /&gt;1. You know it will be messy, so cover your floors/carpet. Make sure you turn/twirl the wax around the applicator to minimize drip. The sleeve helps, but I don&#x27;t think there is a need to buy any extra since it&#x27;s reusable and you will not have much drip on it if you are careful.&lt;br /&gt;2. Have a stop watch/timer! Very important. The instruction says 30 seconds. If it&#x27;s not dry it will be messy, if too long, it&#x27;ll be too hard and painful. Stick to the timing. Do one area at a time if you are a beginner.&lt;br /&gt;3. We al know which is the worst part if you&#x27;re doing brazilian waxing. Be sure to hold firmly onto the back skin (you will be peeling towards you, so hold the part of your skin that is furthest from you) to make sure that you the wax peels off and in time. The part of ths skin is very soft and will tend to lift together with the wax.&lt;br /&gt;4. Wrap a scarf around your mouth if you need to scream. Feels like a security blanket ;)&lt;br /&gt;5. Be sure to have a mirror and a waste bin.&lt;br /&gt;6. Putting pressure on your skin with your fingers after the peel realllllyyy helps!&lt;br /&gt;It is a painful process, but it&#x27;s worth all worth it! Glad I bought it!</li>
